The Severe Flood in Hua County – Soliciting Aid from the Flood Relief Entertainment Event – More Than 9,000 Houses Collapsed, 280,000 People Awaiting Relief; The Disaster Is Severe, the Association Asks the Relief Association to Handle It 128

The Water Disaster Entertainment Association in this city received a telegram from the magistrate of Hua County, Henan Province, and the Water Disaster Association yesterday, stating: "The people of Hua County are unfortunate, and floods are frequent. Fortunately, various charitable organizations in Shanghai have repeatedly provided relief, and the disaster-stricken people have been able to regenerate. However, the accumulated water has just receded, and the early drought has returned. This year, there was a drought for half a year, and the harvest of wheat was reduced. It was not until the beginning of July that the sweet rain began to fall, and the late autumn crops were barely sown. We were happy to see the lush green seedlings, and there was hope for the harvest. Unexpectedly, from the day of Wenri to Youri, it rained continuously, and the flat land was flooded. The germinated autumn crops all died in the water. In addition, accumulated water from Changyuan and Fengqiu counties all entered Hua County, and the Yellow River floods overflowed. Wan River houses and villages collapsed, villages were submerged, and people died. The city gates were surrounded by water on three sides. Yesterday, the provincial government dispatched a committee to the county to investigate the disaster. The county magistrate and others went out to survey, first riding horses and wading through the water, then taking boats, traveling back and forth for several days, traveling more than a hundred miles. Statistics show that more than 600 villages were flooded, of which more than 400 villages in the fifth, sixth, and seventh districts had been hit by the disaster three times. The tragic situation cannot be fully described in writing. We were suffering from a lack of avenues to appeal when we suddenly read in the newspaper that you gentlemen were promoting the kindness of rescuing the drowning, doing the good deed of helping the masses, and launching entertainment to help the disaster relief, universally saving all living beings on the earth. We admire your benevolence, and we are extremely grateful. Therefore, we have attached the disaster situation survey table of this county and photos of the tragic situation of the third-year water disaster, and we hope that you will inspect them and quickly provide rescue. The people of the entire county will be able to survive, and we will be extremely grateful." Signed, Xie Suian, Magistrate of Hua County, and the Water Disaster Association, respectfully. Attached: Disaster Survey Table (1) "Disaster area": The entire county has ten districts, and more than nine districts have been affected by the disaster, with a total area of more than fifty square miles. (2) "Number of deaths": The upper three villages of the East Qingcheng River have been washed away by the Yellow River flood, and there have been many deaths. (3) "Number of mu of submerged farmland": A total of more than 1.8 million mu. (4) "Amount of property loss": Drowned crops, collapsed houses, and other losses are estimated to be worth more than 10 million yuan. (5) "Number of submerged houses": More than 9,000 houses were washed away. (6) "Number of disaster-stricken households": A total of 681 villages, more than 50,000 households. (7) "Number of people awaiting relief": More than 280,000 people. (8) "Number of people displaced due to the disaster": Most of the county has been displaced due to the inconvenience of water, and many live in the open air on the land. (9) "Disaster period": Since the beginning of summer this year, there has been a drought, which has caused a disaster. Until the 7th, 8th, and 9th of July, the rain began to fall, and the autumn crops began to be sown. Suddenly, on the 12th, there was a heavy rainstorm, which did not stop day and night. From the 17th to the 25th, it rained continuously, and the land was flooded. Houses collapsed and crops were submerged. The villages near the dike were also washed away at this time. After receiving the telegram, in addition to replying to the county government, the association has yesterday transferred the original telegram and attached letter to the Relief Association, requesting a way to provide relief.

Chinese Police Officer Wang Yonghao Sues for Usury: Zhang Jingzhi Lived by Lending Money at High Interest; Excessive Oppression Led to Legal Action 130

Zhang Jingzhi, a Tianjin native residing at No. 30, Lane 345, Tangshan Road, has been engaged in the business of lending money at high interest rates, exploiting usury. There are not a few poor people who have been economically oppressed by him. Wang Yonghao, Chinese police officer No. 733 of the Huishan Police Station, once borrowed money from him, but because the interest was too high, he was still unable to repay it. Recently, Zhang sued him in the First Special District Court. Wang was angry at the excessive oppression and, citing the new criminal law's provisions for punishing usury, hired a lawyer to file a criminal complaint against Zhang, requesting legal punishment. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Risheng of the criminal court of the First Special Court opened a court session to summon them. Since the implementation of the new criminal law, this is the second case of prosecuting usury. According to Wang Yonghao's complaint, he borrowed 20 yuan from Zhang in 1920, and Zhang demanded 4 yuan in interest per month. By the following year, according to Zhang's calculation, the principal and interest had reached 120 yuan. In addition, he still owed him 182 yuan in hui money (a type of rotating savings and credit association). However, by 1933, the two amounts had been combined, and together with interest, they had become 694 yuan. The money I repaid was the 15 yuan salary given to me each month by a certain rental agent, which the defendant collected. Up to now, I have repaid more than 400 yuan in succession, etc. When questioned, the defendant Zhang Jingzhi denied that the loan was a loan at a high interest rate, saying that the money owed by the defendant was all lent to him successively, and that the 694 yuan was all principal, with no hui money included, and even less interest on interest. The interest rate was also set at 2% per month, with a promissory note as proof. Because he had delayed in repaying, he had filed a lawsuit in the civil court, etc., and submitted 13 promissory notes. The plaintiff's attorney then stated that the civil court case had been suspended and should be handled after this case is resolved. Judge Huang ruled that since the plaintiff had presented witnesses, saying that he could prove the fact that the defendant was exploiting usury, he adjourned the hearing to investigate the evidence and question it again.

The police department's lawyer, Chen Ming, explained the results of the investigation, and filed a public prosecution based on Article 150 of the Criminal Law (disrupting order), Article 153 (obstructing official duties), and Article 277 (assault). The police also submitted as evidence the broken rifle carried by the Vietnamese constables, the damaged hats, the iron bars and stones used in the assault, and the flags with slogans. Furthermore, Witness No. 632, a Chinese constable, testified that the first defendant, Xue Ruxu, used a wooden stick to hit people. Witness No. 422, a Chinese constable, testified that the third defendant, Xu Xiaosi, held a flag and shouted slogans, and also beat a Vietnamese constable. Witness No. 29, a Western constable, testified that he saw two Chinese constables chasing the second defendant, Li Yuehua, so he helped to arrest Li. At this point, Judge Sun stated that the police department's prosecution of the defendants for assault was a private prosecution, requiring the injured Vietnamese constables to appear in court for cross-examination before a verdict could be reached. Currently, the injured Vietnamese constables are receiving treatment in the hospital, and the case cannot proceed. Therefore, the hearing was adjourned to the morning of the 28th. The defendants were returned to the detention center.

Hua Azeng, the owner of the Huangdai Watermelon Company in Xiyuan, received two threatening letters from the "Communist Party Reconnaissance Team Captain Zhou Gengsheng" starting on the 10th of this month, attempting to extort 10,000 yuan. Yesterday morning, they were prosecuted in the First Special Court under Article 346, Section 3 of the Criminal Law. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the case, saying that Hua Azeng, in addition to operating the Huangdai Watermelon Company, also contracted tea stalls in the Yong'an and Xianshi amusement parks, with a good business, which attracted the attention of bandits. Around 2 PM on the 10th of this month, Hua received a threatening letter, signed by Zhou Gengsheng, the captain of the Communist Party Reconnaissance Team, demanding 10,000 yuan in "subsidy funds." If not granted, Hua's descendants would be killed, and reporting to the police was forbidden. Hua immediately reported the letter to the police. After a detailed investigation, the police learned that the letter was mailed from a mailbox on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. On August 16th, Hua received a second letter. Knowing it was a threatening letter, Hua refused to accept it and had the postman return it. The police have since retrieved the letter from the post office. The letter urged Hua to contact them quickly. Yesterday morning, detective Shang Wu learned that the bandits were hiding in the Deyuelou Teahouse on North Xizang Road, so he arrested the two defendants. Two receipts for mailing letters were found on Wang Asheng. Wang Zhixiang confessed to the police that he wrote the draft of the letter and instructed Wang Asheng to mail it, but the idea originated with a man named Li who is still at large. Li used to work for Hua Azeng and discussed the threatening wording in room 13 of the Dongxin Hotel, which Wang Zhixiang then wrote down. Because further investigation is needed, the police requested an extension. Judge Liu Yugui briefly questioned the two defendants and ordered them to be detained for further questioning in ten days.

Dong Zhenyi Throws Himself into the Huangpu River - Owes Over 1,000 Yuan to Indians - Drove to Desperation and Suicide 133

At 5 PM the day before yesterday, near the Dinghai Bridge in Yangshupu East, a middle-aged man in a Western suit was seen pacing on the Bund. In a flash, the man disappeared, leaving behind a white sun helmet and a brown serge jacket. Assuming he went ashore, the area was sparsely populated, and he would have been visible. Therefore, they suspected he had thrown himself into the river and died. They immediately sent the belongings to the Customs Water Police Station. Inside, the name "Dong Zhenyi" was written on the leather belt with a pen. Two business cards were found in the pocket, one from the Chengji Hospital in Gaochangqiao and one from Shi Ruihua of the Xinghua Printing Bureau in Hongdeli, Xiamen Road. The police, with leads to follow, immediately dispatched detective Yao Guofa to investigate. They learned that the deceased was indeed named Dong Zhenyi, 30 years old, from Changzhou, living in a house without a number on Pingliang Road, Xiajiabang. Dong had worked as a director in a department of the Shenxin No. 6 Factory, proficient in writing. After losing his job, he was now selling medicines for Chengji Hospital. His wife had passed away, and he remarried a woman named Li last year, and they were deeply in love. According to Li, her husband was very concerned with appearances. Even though his monthly income was very small after leaving the Shenxin Factory, he still took a private rickshaw every day, and his clothing was no less than before, causing increasing financial difficulties. He owed over 1,000 yuan to Indians and other creditors. On the 16th of this month, he gave her one yuan, asking her to use it for several days of living expenses. He said he was going out to find work, but he had not returned for several nights and must have committed suicide. She was heartbroken. The detective, having clarified the matter, returned to the police station to report, in order to recover the body.

Jin Yu Securities Firm Embezzlement of Treasury Bonds Case Closed Yesterday - Gan Denglai Resort to Embezzlement After Public Debt Investment Failed - Wei Yuansheng Was Implicated by a Friend, Lawyer Delivered Eloquent Speech 135

Gan Denglai of Yuyao, an employee of the Jin Yu Securities Firm on Qingyuan Lane, Beijing Road, privately traded public debt using fabricated accounts, incurring losses of over ten thousand yuan. Fearing to suffer the same fate as his colleague, surnamed Pan, who was reported to the police by the firm's manager, Gan Yunqiao, for corruption, he sought help from Wei Tingrong's son, Yuansheng, but was refused. He then took advantage of the gap before the end of July's settlement to steal a large amount of treasury bonds bearing the firm's stamp. Details were reported in the previous issue. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide of the First Special District Court continued the hearing.

On the way, he was swindled out of 1,200 yuan, and spent 40 yuan in expenses, leaving 1,060 yuan. He was instructed to bury the remaining money and treasury bonds under a certain pagoda. The team leader rushed to the address and found 760 yuan in cash and 4,000 yuan in treasury bonds. Wang Xinquan was nowhere to be found. The court then questioned the defendant, Gan Denglai, who confessed that due to public debt trading, he had incurred huge losses. He had asked Wei Yuansheng for help, but Wei had refused. On the 29th, he went to Wei's house to ask for a few days of lodging. Later, Wei Yuansheng, seeing the advertisement posted by Gan Yunqiao to apprehend him, urged him to surrender to the police quickly. Regarding the private trading of public debt at Jin Yu, he fabricated five accounts, three of which were real people, and he only borrowed their names for public debt transactions. The other two accounts, Xian Ji and Nian Ji, were entirely fabricated. Seeing that his colleague Pan Quan Zhong was reported to the police by the manager for corruption, he thought he also had corrupt practices, fearing that he would be treated the same as Pan, he seized the opportunity to steal the bonds and escape.

Wei Yuansheng testified that when Qian came to his house on July 27th, he only said that he would be going to his hometown and asked to stay for a few days. Unable to refuse, he agreed. On the 29th, he brought a leather suitcase and lived on the third floor of his house, not knowing that the case contained treasury bonds. Later, seeing the newspaper, he forced him to surrender to the police and hired a car, instructing the driver to take him to the police station. Before leaving, Qian wanted to take all his cash, but I feared that he would take the money and escape, so I withheld the money. Later, the detectives came to my house to investigate the stolen treasury bonds and found 25,000 yuan in the Qian's bedroom, which was handed over to the detectives. The next morning, they continued to search the room and found 20,000 yuan in treasury bonds under the mat, which was also handed over to the police. Because the facts were clear, the court ordered the debate to begin. First, the police stated that the defendant, Gan Denglai, had originally worked at Jin Yu. He had been fired last year and re-employed this spring at the request of others. He continued to fabricate names, privately print orders, and forge seals, committing fraud as before. Seeing that the case of his colleague, Pan, was exposed, fearing that he would suffer the same fate as Pan, he seized the opportunity to steal the bonds and escape. His escape can be said to be influenced by Pan. The fact that he withdrew his money from the Agricultural and Industrial Bank showed that he had planned in advance. The implication of Wei Yuansheng was purely due to Qian's confession. However, Qian has now admitted that his surrender was advocated by Wei. Therefore, the degree of suspicion borne by Wei has been greatly reduced, and it should be judged according to law. Next, Wu Linkun, the lawyer representing Jin Yu, stated the object of the private prosecution against Gan Denglai: (1) 1,000 yuan in treasury bonds; (2) 1,540 yuan in cash; (3) Qian fabricated client's private trading of public debt owing 2,832 yuan and 85 cents. Finally, lawyer Jiang Yiping defended Wei Yuansheng, saying that Wei was unfortunately falsely accused by Qian, resulting in his being in the position of a defendant. Viewing the allegations involving Wei in Gan's confession, there are many contradictions, making them difficult to believe. For example, Qian said that on the 27th, he told Wei that he would collect the public debt from the bank on the 29th. The manager of the firm would never tell Qian about the collection of public debt two days in advance. If he did not know, how could he tell Wei? This is the first point. Gan also confessed that he gave the treasury bonds to Wei when he arrived at Wei's house. Qian's theft of the bonds was due to failed speculation, incurring huge losses. Why would Qian, even at the risk of breaking the law, easily give the illegally obtained property to others? Qian is not so foolish, he would never do this. This is the second point. Supposing Wei knew about Qian's illegal behavior and was willing to help, he would never urge him to surrender to the police, but let him escape. And Wei could have hoarded the treasury bonds. Instead, Wei not only urged Qian to surrender, but also hired a car to take him to the police station. At the same time, he intercepted the cash that Qian wanted to take away. Because Qian wanted to escape but could not, his entire plan was ruined by Wei. He hated Wei very much, so he falsely accused Wei of conspiracy to the police. This is the third point. As for Wei's allowing Qian to stay temporarily, it was a normal act of friendship and it was not proper to question him in advance. Upon seeing the newspaper report, he resolutely gave the plaintiff various assistance, so as to minimize the illegal damage. Wei's attitude is bright and his actions are upright. Not only is he innocent, but he is also meritorious. Now, he is involved in a public prosecution. For the sake of justice, Wei Yuansheng should be declared innocent, so that those who support justice in the world will not be discouraged. This was a powerful and eloquent defense, quite moving to the court. After the opening of the court, the judge ordered Gan Denglai to be detained and Wei Yuansheng to remain on bail from the original shop, pending sentencing next Wednesday.

New Factory of the Zhonghua Book Company Completed - China's Only Printing Factory 137

The old factory of the Zhonghua Book Company on Jing'an Temple Road was completed twenty years ago, and is not very suitable in the current era. Therefore, the old factory was sold and a new factory was built on Gordon Road and Macao Road, with five four-story buildings, about three million cubic feet. Its characteristics are four: (1) All steel and concrete construction, extremely sturdy, load-bearing, and fireproof, all very suitable. (2) Each room uses steel windows, the area of the windows accounting for two-thirds of the walls, sufficient light and air. (3) The factory uses a "川" shape, with the offices built horizontally on top of the "川" shape, the printing plant on the lower floor, the general office on the second floor, the editorial office on the third floor, and the library and testing room on the fourth floor. The entrances and exits are very economical. The general manager can gather the cadres and staff in one minute, and can gather the heads of the various departments in three minutes. Other work connections are also very time-saving. (4) The printing capacity is increased, and the efficiency is increased. Daily letterpress can print 10 million pages of books, color printing can print more than one million New Year's prints of various sizes, and intaglio printing can print more than one million banknotes. In addition, various printing techniques, such as photogravure, photographic plate, electroplating plate, carved relief plate, and Western typesetting, are all the most sophisticated and up-to-date. The relocation is scheduled to begin next month, and new machines will be installed, but work will not be stopped. The entire move is expected to be completed by the end of the year. Whether in terms of architecture or output, it is almost the only printing factory in China.

The details are as follows:

Letter to the Relief Association

To the esteemed: Since the beginning of this summer, continuous rain has been rampant, mountain floods have erupted, the Yangtze River has overflowed first, and the Yellow River has breached its dikes afterwards. The disaster area is wide, and the disaster is heavier than in the past. We, as fellow citizens, cannot but feel grief for this great disaster and calamity. Therefore, we have boldly initiated a flood relief entertainment fair, incorporating charity into entertainment, and raising funds through entertainment. In the future, all surplus funds will be handed over to your association for distribution to the disaster areas to help the victims. We know that a cup of water or a cart of firewood cannot solve the problem, but accumulating bits and pieces and gathering sand into a tower may provide some help to the victims. Now that our fair has just opened, we plan to invite members of your association to be stationed here to provide guidance, so that we can follow your lead to benefit the disaster and revitalize affairs. We are truly grateful to the public.

Around 8 AM on the 11th of this month, two rogue Russians, Konstantin Dinashav and Airahanqin, went to the home of Englishman Tom Boson at No. 810 Avenue Lafayette in the French Concession to take out 600 yuan in ten-yuan banknotes from the Tianjin Local Bank, offering to sell them for 200 yuan. Yesterday morning at 11 AM, Judge Li of the Second Special Court continued the hearing in the First Criminal Court. The police lawyer said that because the investigation of the case was not concluded, he requested another adjournment. The judge questioned the Western detective in charge of the case whether he had sent official letters to Harbin, Tianjin, etc. for investigation. The detective replied that the letters were sent by the police station and had not yet received a reply. At this time, the defense lawyer hired by the defendants requested the court to have the injuries on the defendants photographed and filed for record. The judge said that this could be requested from the police department and announced that the case would be re-heard on the 23rd in a special court. The defendants were returned to the detention center.

Mr. Chen and his men spotted him and, unwilling to let him go easily, rushed forward with axes. Autopsy Report of a Russian Suicide 144

Wan Mu Ai Hua Wei Qu Xisai (transliteration), a 38-year-old Russian employee of the World Detective Protection Office located in Room 310, No. 2 Beijing Road, was addicted to gambling. Recently, he embezzled a significant amount of public funds from the office for gambling debts, which he could not repay. In a fit of resentment, he conceived the idea of ending his life. Yesterday morning around nine o'clock, while no one was around, he used his own pistol to shoot himself in the head inside the office. He collapsed in a pool of blood. The office's chief supervisor, an Englishman named Ge Like, returned from outside and discovered the body. He immediately reported the incident to the Central Police Station, which dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. The detectives transported the Russian to Gongji Hospital, but resuscitation attempts failed, and he soon died. The detectives also found three suicide notes near his body, stating that he was driven to suicide by financial difficulties. The body was then taken to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Wei was appointed by the First Special District Court to conduct an autopsy. After Head Constable Lu Dagong and others explained the situation, and Ge Like testified that the deceased was his assistant and that he was not present when the suicide occurred. "Upon my return, a Western woman told me that she had heard a gunshot from within my writing room. I intended to go inside to investigate but found that the door had been locked from the inside by the deceased. I broke the glass in a small window next to the door and managed to open the door, finding the deceased collapsed between two chairs with a lot of blood flowing from his head, and the pistol lying beside his body on the right side. I then notified the police station. As for the funds he used, I am unable to determine the amount at this time as he was in charge of the accounting books, etc.," Ge Like said. The deceased's wife, He Ai Tuo, also testified. Prosecutor Guo Wei concluded that the deceased, Russian man Wan Mu Ai Hua Wei Qu Xisai, male, died from a gunshot wound to the head sustained during his lifetime. The body was released to Ge Like for preparation for burial with a signed guarantee.

Since its founding, it has recorded over ten thousand items, making it extremely convenient for checking past and present periodical materials. The original major event category table will now include the source of each event, as well as the publication date and page number of various newspapers and periodicals, so that one monthly magazine serves both as a periodical index and a daily newspaper index, making it extremely convenient to check. Now, to facilitate readers' reference to materials, the journal has reached an agreement with the Hongying Library, which is related to the society. The magazine and newspaper index directory referenced by the journal can be inspected at the library. Those who subscribe to a copy of the journal this year will receive a reading certificate from the society to Hongying Library, for the purpose of inspecting magazines and newspapers at the library. In terms of writing in this issue, Yang Jun's "Drought Disasters Since the Republic of China," Jiang Weiqiao's "Modern Buddhist Trends," Bai Jiao's "The Tragedy of Concubine Zhen," and Liang Yuandong's "Reading Abstracts" and the introduction to "History of the Gradual Easternization of Europeanization" are all exceptionally rich and valuable. As for the magazine's main points index, this issue records a total of four thousand two hundred and seventy items, with more abundant materials than before.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 159

— (Wan Lu)

Everything has a prominent side and a dark side. Ordinary people only see the prominent side and do not study its dark side. Smart people see the prominent side while also exploring the dark side. There is another type of person who is the opposite of ordinary people, only seeing the dark side and ignoring the prominent side. The views of ordinary people are naturally too shallow, but focusing only on the dark side is also too disappointing. Only those who see both sides will not be fooled, nor will they be disappointed. Take Shanghai for example, simply admiring the brilliance of neon lights is not recognizing Shanghai. Exclusively studying how many stores have closed on Nanjing Road and how many suicides are reported in the newspaper every day is also not the correct way to understand Shanghai. Therefore, you must see both sides to be considered smart and to truly understand Shanghai.

The best things in the world have a bit of confusion in them, making them more interesting. If you see everything through, there is no fun at all. For example, when you are in the midst of sweet affection, suddenly the image of a decaying skeleton pops into your head, sending a chill down your spine and instantly scattering all the tenderness to the clouds. Or, if you are calculating when a sum of money is due, or when a property should be settled, with your mind filled with colorful banknotes, you suddenly think about the impermanence of life, when everything comes to an end, and your whole spirit sinks to the lowest point. Therefore, it is said: a bit of confusion brings a bit of happiness; more intelligence brings more torment.

From Flood Control to Afforestation 160

— Gu Foying from Tokyo

Domestic newspapers report that a foreign water conservancy expert said that China's recent flood control methods, which focus on dikes, are not a good strategy. In the future, more attention should be paid to dredging. This is certainly true, but dredging is still a temporary solution. The fundamental method of flood control is afforestation because trees can conserve water and regulate climate. This is a very simple principle and need not be explained further.

On this trip to Japan, I paid special attention to their forestry policies. I visited several forest farms and even climbed several mountains in Hokkaido. I collected many plans, reports, and forms from the Hokkaido Prefectural Government and the Colonial Department in Sapporo. After careful study, I realized that it is a big mistake for China to imitate Japan's current forestry facilities completely. Their area is small, funding is sufficient, talent is abundant, and they already have considerable achievements. Now they are naturally only conducting trials, research, and improvement work. However, in China, the situation is exactly the opposite. The government leaves millions of barren hills unplanted and only learns from them how to run trial farms. Regardless of the success or failure of these farms, even if you discover after ten or twenty years how much water a certain type of tree absorbs and how much it evaporates, perhaps a flood has already sent your trial farm to a watery grave. When you are hungry, you should fill your stomach with large pancakes and fried dough sticks first. It is okay to study the manufacturing methods of sponge cake later.

My point is that the government only needs to make a decision, roughly formulate an implementation outline, (just roughly, because seeking precision will inevitably lead to disputes, and in fact, cold-climate tree species do not necessarily die when brought to warm climates). For example, it should specify which types of trees should be planted in certain areas, issue orders nationwide, and set up a nursery in each designated area. One or two years later, when the seedlings are cultivated, a nationwide mobilization should be launched, requiring each person to plant a certain number of trees, with heavy penalties for those who violate the rules. Even if each person only plants ten trees, with four hundred million people, there would be four billion trees. If each tree occupies one square zhang, there would be over six hundred million mu of land, and the required funding is actually minimal. Frankly speaking, everyone knows how to plant trees. It does not require skilled techniques like operating machinery, nor does it require precise management like growing vegetables. As long as you plant them and do not pull them up, they will grow on their own. If China has large forest farms of over six hundred million mu, the disasters of floods and droughts will be reduced by at least half in twenty years. I can guarantee this based on scientific principles. As for the forest experts for trial research, we will naturally need to rely on them in the future, but you need to have hair before you can use a comb.

Dajiao (Taoist Ritual) 161

— Yan Bokuang

Although efforts are being made to reform various useless things in society, the public's superstitious belief in divine power remains firmly entrenched, posing a major obstacle to social reformers!

It is not easy to achieve rapid results in promoting changes in customs. The Shanghai Public Security Bureau and Social Affairs Bureau have been working hard to eliminate superstition for many years, but in the middle of July, the atmosphere of Dajiao rituals at the entrances of various alleys is still rampant, both in the east and in the west. It is truly helpless! It is a great pity to waste so much useful money in the ethereal realm.

The amount of money wasted in Shanghai alone is considerable. The total amount of money wasted on superstition nationwide is staggering. This year, they are reiterating the ban, earnestly persuading the public not to engage in these useless activities, hoping that this trend can be slightly reduced. In various towns and villages outside of Shanghai, during this ghost month of July, the sounds of drums and cymbals and the smoke of incense can be seen everywhere. Even larger amounts of paper money are burned, supposedly to help homeless ghosts and prevent them from haunting people, and to ensure the safety of the population. This is truly absurdly ridiculous.

Last year, there was a severe drought; this year, there is a major flood, leaving disaster victims stranded and with nowhere to go. Closing my eyes and thinking, I feel that so many disaster victims are in urgent need of relief. Now everyone should be frugal and save money to help the disaster victims. Wouldn't it be more virtuous to use the money spent on Dajiao nationwide for disaster relief? I am willing to speak out for the disaster victims and hope that everyone will stand up and promote this!

Questions and Answers on the Flood 162

— (Ning Ziqiang)

Zilu asked Confucius, "How is the water situation this year?" Confucius said, "The overflowing waters are everywhere under the heavens."

Zilu then asked, "Is such a great flood beneficial to farming?" Confucius said, "Water! Water! (Disaster!) What good can be derived from water?"

Zilu further asked, "Is the flood receding these days?" Confucius said, "It passes on like this, never ceasing day and night."

Zilu asked again, "Since the flood is receding so quickly, are the seedlings unharmed?" Confucius said, "There are those that sprout but do not flower, and those that flower but bear no fruit!"

The Rotating Cylinder in Front of Barber Shops 163

— Wu Aibo

When we usually pass by a barber shop, don't we see a three-colored cylinder rotating there non-stop? This three-colored cylinder is the unique symbol of a barber shop, and everyone knows it. However, to delve into its origins, I'm afraid many people don't quite understand.

A few days ago, I went to a used bookstore for a chat and inadvertently saw a book called "Observations on Travel in America," written by Mr. Wang Yizhi. At the beginning of the book, there were photos and prefaces by Mr. Shi Liangcai, the former general manager of this newspaper, and Mr. Chen Leng, which aroused my curiosity, so I opened it to take a look. On page 134 of this book, Mr. Wang discussed this matter, and his explanation is as follows:

"The constantly rotating cylinder in front of barber shops is painted around with what looks like red, white, and black stripes, spiraling upwards. Once it is set in motion by electricity, it is most eye-catching. This custom was introduced from Europe. In ancient Europe, barbers often also served as surgeons. The reason why this constantly rotating cylinder has red, white, and black stripes is that in ancient times, doctors used various colored cloths for binding wounds, which were often torn into very thin strips. You can get a glimpse of this in the bandages used in hospitals today."

The above is what Mr. Wang Yizhi said, which seems very detailed. I wonder if there are any other explanations. This is to ask the readers for guidance.

Little Western Paradise 164

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seventeen: Mo Wen's Daughter Has Unspeakable Pain, Everyone Eagerly Looks at the Dignitary, Admiring His Noble Demeanor

However, standing next to him was a woman, only in her thirties, with a perm, wearing high heels, and a tight cheongsam that stretched smoothly over the instep of her feet, very fashionable. Everyone couldn't help but feel disappointed when they saw this, never expecting that the grand welcome was just to welcome such a gentleman. However, Zhang Jiefu's psychology was the opposite of ordinary people's. He was even more enthusiastic. From afar, he saw the special commissioner's car arriving, his face beaming with red, and he took off his hat, standing by the gate, with his hands hanging straight down. Seeing that Special Commissioner Lan was about to reach the gate, he didn't dare to be negligent and immediately rushed forward, facing him directly, and bowing deeply three times. The special commissioner was a little surprised to suddenly see someone rushing forward to salute, but he guessed that it was probably a local welcoming representative, and definitely not someone trying to intercept him to file a complaint. Therefore, in his busy schedule, he stood still and nodded twice in succession. Jiefu saw him stop and nod twice, and his heart blossomed. He bent over, smiling, and took out a business card from his pocket, holding it up and handing it over. Special Commissioner Lan took it and looked at it. It was an unfamiliar name, and there was no official title. He didn't know which department it was from, so he just said "Oh" and nodded, saying, "Let's talk in detail later." Jiefu said "Yes, yes" twice, and stepped back two steps. Special Commissioner Lan accompanied his wife and walked into Little Western Paradise, and Jiefu also followed inside. This time, it felt like the bones in his body immediately gained several pounds, and he walked with very steady steps. He looked at the people watching the excitement on both sides, and his chest puffed out, as if hinting to people, "Look, I'm walking with the special commissioner." Especially when he walked into Little Western Paradise and saw a group of acquaintances, he couldn't stop smiling from the corners of his mouth. The meaning was again, "My welcoming Special Commissioner Lan is not accidental, right?" Because of this, others indeed believed that he was a relative of Special Commissioner Lan. (296)

Records of Fleeting Fragrances 165

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

"After the flower juice is made, we use newly spun silk from that year (of course, undyed white silk)," she said again, "We press it into square shapes like mooncakes; their size is determined by the diameter of my rouge container, so they fit perfectly. These square pieces of silk floss must be soaked in the flower juice for at least five or six days to be completely saturated; once they are saturated, we take them out one by one and put them in the sunlight to dry. After about three or four days of drying, when they are completely dry, we can send them in for us to use. The effort involved is quite a lot when you calculate it carefully, but fortunately, we don't waste it too much. Each time we make it, it's enough for five or six months!"

How did the Empress Dowager apply rouge?

She first soaked a small square of red silk floss in a cup of warm water, then took it out and gently rubbed it in the palms of her hands until she felt satisfied. Because women in the past always applied a lot of red to the palms of their hands, the Empress Dowager's first step was to apply it to her palms. After applying it to her palms, she applied it to her cheeks. At this time, she didn't have time to talk to me anymore. She brought her face very close to the mirror and applied it with extreme care, hoping that it wouldn't be too thick or too uneven, just right. The last step was to apply it to her lips; however, people in the past definitely didn't apply lipstick to the entire upper and lower lips like people do now. They only applied a little rouge to the middle of the lips, probably influenced by the phrase "cherry mouth" used by scholars. (396)

Casual Talk

Tan Biscuits 166

— Xue Jiqun

A few days ago, I was socializing at a relative's house, and during the meal, a Mr. Wang who works in the food industry chatted with me. He said: "Business is really difficult to do now. Customers are becoming more and more discerning, and costs are increasing year by year. No matter what product it is, whether it's produced by our food company, invented by ourselves, copied from Western production, or a famous specialty from the Jiangsu and Zhejiang areas, nowadays, not to mention competitors trying to grab business, even those who specialize in wholesale or selling imported goods, once they hear that a certain business is profitable, they will copy each other. On the customer's side, there is competition between companies, so they compare and naturally the superior wins and the inferior is eliminated, and everyone goes to the better company. However, if we put ourselves in the position of doing this business, then we will have to cry in pain. At the moment, not to mention anything else, just take the biscuit business in Shanghai as an example. Biscuits are also a 'big deal' in the food industry. Small capital can't do it well. In the past, apart from the imported goods in tins, there are two foreign companies in Shanghai that have factories here, such as 'Sullivan,' etc. On the domestic side, there are 'Mashen,' 'Taifeng,' 'Taikang,' 'Guanshengyuan,' etc., which are relatively large in scope, produce a lot, and their sales are not bad. Speaking of Guanshengyuan, we now know that more than ten years ago, it was still a small shop in Nine Acres, specializing in preserved tangerine peel and concentrated beef juice. Who knew that in less than twenty years, it has grown from one store to several, from Shanghai to Suzhou, Hangzhou, Ningbo, Hankou, Beijing, Tianjin, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, with no less than ten branches, distributing to more than a hundred places. The business is booming, and the capital has increased to 500,000 yuan. Their factory has always been on Jumen Road in South Shanghai. General Manager Xian Guansheng is hardworking and frugal, and has been like this for decades. No matter what the matter, or even a small product, he must personally try it and personally study it. For the sake of improving the quality of candies and biscuits, he and Wang Changyuan, the director of the biscuit department in the factory, have even gone to the Three Islands several times for inspection. Realizing that the factory base was insufficient and that the efficiency of manual labor was far inferior to that of mechanized production, he bought more than forty acres of land in Caohejing two years ago, half of which was used as a farm, and half of which was used to build a five-story steel and concrete mansion. He also ordered the latest and most economical machine from France. After a long period of planning and operation, it has now been successfully completed. Factory supervisor Zhao Zemin and Mr. Xian go to Caohejing every day. At the moment, the biscuit department has been moved from the old factory, the machines have been installed, and several specialized technicians have been hired to start the machines, and the products are excellent. According to the responsible talk of Mr. Wang Changyuan, for example, originally one ton of coal was used every day, and only 1,000 pounds of biscuits were baked. Now, since the new machine has been tested, it's too cheap. One ton of coal can be used for three or four days, and the fine biscuits produced are thoroughly baked, quickly made, have heavy ingredients, and taste good, with five times more products than before, while the coal consumption is reduced by 60-70%, and labor is also saved, so the cost is relatively low. In terms of products, there are no less than twenty or thirty kinds, such as morning tea, milk, sandwich, soda, etc. Their pricing is based on the principle of small profits and quick turnover. The raw materials are increasing step by step, and the taste is moderate and balanced. Although they cannot boast of being unique, they regard imported products as a strong enemy.

Aren't we hearing about the economic downturn all around us? Who knew that in this trend, there would be such a Guanshengyuan biscuit factory expanding and developing, which is worthy of promotion and introduction. In this way, we hope that their products will continue to move forward, and then the achievement of their future is immeasurable, and we hope that other domestic manufacturers can follow their example of hard work, focusing on their own efforts, without making unfounded exaggerations, then Mr. Sun Yat-sen's "People's Livelihood" doctrine will not be difficult to realize.

After Mr. Wang finished speaking, I was happy to write it down.

Education News

The Problem of Co-educational Schools in Peiping is Completely Solved. The Original Female Students of Each School Will Be Graduated Yearly. No Female Students Will Be Enrolled in the First Grade This Year. 167

(Special Dispatch from Peiping) The problem of abolishing private co-educational schools in Peiping has taken a sharp turn after mediation from various parties in recent days. Both parties have agreed on a general outline for resolution. The Private Middle School Federation held a general membership meeting at 11:00 AM on the 19th at the Senlong Western Restaurant in the Dong'an Market to discuss detailed solutions in order to make a final decision. Representatives from 52 schools were present at the meeting. After lunch, the five executive committee members who had visited the authorities reported on the agreed outline, which was then discussed. The entire body unanimously passed the proposal. After the meeting, all members of the federation took cars to visit Yuan Liang at the Municipal Government. After some discussion and explanation, three solutions were decided: (1) The original female students of the co-educational schools will continue their studies at their original schools and graduate yearly; (2) The first grade of junior high school and the first grade of senior high school in each school this year will not be allowed to enroll female students. The names of the female students who have already been enrolled will be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau, which will find ways to place them in other public and private girls' middle schools in Peiping; (3) The Private Middle School Federation will draft a formal document and submit it to the authorities. After approval, it will be implemented. The members of the Private Middle School Federation left the Municipal Government at around 4:00 PM.

Difficulty in Placing Female Students

The private Kongde Middle School is also co-educational, and the students learn French, not English. Ordinary private middle schools in Peiping all teach English. The first-year junior high school students of the school who are graduates of Kongde Elementary School also study French, which raises doubts about the second article of the co-educational solution. Kongde Middle School is also one of the private middle schools. According to the second article, the school is also not allowed to enroll female students. Then how should the female graduates of Kongde Elementary School be placed? Can the names of the female students already enrolled in Kongde Middle School also be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau? Will the Social Affairs Bureau be able to find ways to place them in other public and private girls' middle schools in Peiping? (Jin)

The Government of Dutch Borneo Burned Chinese Books. The Words in the Books Were Considered to Violate the Law. The Teachers of the Shanmu School Were Expelled from the Country. 168

The government of Dutch West Borneo recently judged that the teachers of the Shanmu School in Kunshan (doulrouok) improperly revised the spelling of students, and was ordered by the Han Affairs Department of Java to be expelled from the country, and burned our country's textbooks, and strictly inspected the entry of Chinese books. After the Chinese Overseas United Association was reported, it was very indignant and will express its views. The reporter of the Industrial News Agency learned the whole story and recorded it in detail below.

Chinese Children's Composition Considered Inappropriate

The Shanmu School in Kunshan was founded by the Catholic Church. A few days ago, the Minister of the Political Department of the area and a translator went to the school to investigate and found that some of the students' compositions revised by the teachers were considered "uncontrolled," "words were intense," and "contained political provocation and malice to alienate various ethnic groups." The composition topics were "Unity" and "Banning Foreign Goods." There were inappropriate words in the students' compositions such as "Eastern × ghosts." There were also several student question-and-answer books that were considered to have harmed the feelings of various ethnic groups. The Minister of the Political Department immediately questioned the teachers, who explained that the questions were contained in the textbooks and were not invented by individuals.

Strict Inspection of Chinese Textbooks

The Political Department further inspected the textbooks and sent the Advanced Book II and Book IV of the Chinese textbooks used by the school and the Elementary Book VIII to the Han Affairs Department of Java for verification. It then instructed the Minister of the Political Department of Kunshan to collect the Advanced Book III Book I and the Elementary Book III, V, and VII of the Chinese textbooks of the school and send them to Java for review, and reported the situation to the Han Affairs Department for verification.

Burning Books and Expelling Teachers

The Han Affairs Department of Java reviewed the results and considered that the content of the textbooks violated local laws, and ordered the Political Department of Kunshan to confiscate all Chinese textbooks in the school, destroy them on a regular basis, and order the composition teacher to leave the country by a certain date. This announcement has been conveyed to the teachers and school authorities by the local officials of Kunshan. The Shanmu School is an educational institution of the Catholic Church in Kunshan, located in the Yichangxing Building at Lantinwei. The principal is Tan Zhengdao, a Dutch priest, who has specialized in Chaozhou dialect for two years in Chaozhou. The students are all Chinese, and most of the teachers come from Shantou.

More Stringent Inspection of Imported Chinese Books

The shipment of Chinese books to Kunshan has always had two inspection agencies. All imported books and newspapers are first reviewed by the customs wharf. If they are considered inappropriate, they will be detained. After the inspection, they are submitted to the Political Department for inspection. The local area cannot be said to be not strict in monitoring the import of books and newspapers. According to reports, the textbooks used by the Shanmu School were compiled and printed by the Catholic Church of Xujiahui in this city, so they were not inspected by the customs wharf and the Political Department when they entered. Because the Catholic priests in the area have always been respected by the society, but since the occurrence of this case, it is reported that the local area will strictly inspect the entry of Chinese books.

The Jiangsu Education Department Strictly Orders Education Commissioners of Various Counties to Depart for Inspection and Report the Names of Schools and Social Education Institutions in the School District 173

The Jiangsu Provincial Education Department yesterday issued a notice to the Education Bureaus of Shanghai and other counties, saying that the Education Commissioners of the Education Bureaus of each county are required to inspect the educational institutions in their districts at least twice each semester. The newly promulgated regulations have clearly stipulated that the county magistrates and education bureau directors should strictly supervise the education commissioners to set off for inspections on schedule and must earnestly guide and improve them, and must not perfunctorily engage in them. At the same time, all schools and institutions are instructed to submit a report of type A on the mutual supervision method, in addition to submitting it to the bureau. Fill in one more copy, change the word "Director" on the sheet to "Hall Director", and indicate the county and send it directly to the Second Section of this county for verification. There is no need to prepare a text when sending the sheet, so as to simplify it. Each county bureau should also submit a list of the names of the schools and social education institutions under the jurisdiction of each school district to the hall for reference before the opening of the first semester of this year, and do not delay it. The Railway Department Ordered the Two Railways to Promote Literacy Education for Employees and Complete it Within Two Years 179

In order to promote the literacy movement for railway employees, the Ministry of Railways specially appointed commissioners to investigate the education situation of employees in various state-owned railways and formulated measures to promote education for railway employees. After the two railways were implemented, they immediately formulated measures and stipulated that all employees under the age of 40 must receive compulsory literacy education, from August of this year to the end of July of next year as the first implementation period, and from August of next year to the end of July of the following year as the second period. Employee education will be completed within these two years.

News from the Youth Cycling Touring Group 192

The Shanghai Youth Cycling Touring Group is composed entirely of formal businessmen who enjoy long-distance cycling. Therefore, they plan to take long-distance trips to the suburbs with a few like-minded comrades every weekend. I recall that on September 8th of last year, they traveled to Hangzhou along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway by bicycle, taking a total of eleven hours to reach their destination. Now, taking advantage of the completion of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway, they made their first cycling trip on the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway on the weekend of August 18th. Due to the rough and uneven road surface, it took them more than eight hours to reach Wuxi. At first, they thought that the highway, being newly completed, would definitely be flat, so they expected to arrive in about six hours. Now, it took more than two hours extra, which is really disappointing. (For details, please read the English "Shanghai Times" on August 20th, in the sports news column, there is a detailed record of our seven trips.) Although, I feel that this trip was very interesting and I was not discouraged by the difficult roads. Therefore, I have already begun to prepare a cycling club, hoping to unite many comrades and often take long trips on weekends. The purpose of the club is to bring together a few people to have fun, and to help each other, encourage each other, and strive forward, which is conducive to progress, without comparing speed or deciding competition skills. If our country's highways are completed one by one, we may not be able to find a way to travel all over them. This all depends on our spirit and perseverance. During the current preparations, each aspect is not yet perfect, and we rely on the instructions of the comrades to achieve success. No membership fee is charged, as it is entirely an amateur nature, which is completely different from the purpose of other established clubs. However, members should each have a bicycle, which should not be too old or damaged, as it is feared that repairs along the way will be inconvenient for both the group and themselves. Also, those who can continue to ride for two or three hours can join the club. The club is scheduled to go to Wusong on August 25th (Sunday) (postponed if it rains), and will gather at the entrance of the Hongkou Swimming Pool from 6:00 to 6:30 in the morning. Those who are late will not be waited for. If you are unable to participate this Sunday (August 25th), you can fill out the attached paper and send it to our club at China Post Box 256. It is also planned to travel to Kunshan on September 1st (Sunday). Details will be announced later.
